DeMille Award</a> for "Lifetime Achievement in Motion Pictures"</li>\n<li>1960: Inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_actors_with_Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame_motion_picture_stars" title="List of actors with Hollywood Walk of Fame motion picture stars">motion pictures star</a> at 6756 <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Boulevard" title="Hollywood Boulevard">Hollywood Boulevard</a> for his contributions to the film industry.<sup id="cite_ref-HWOF_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HWOF-47">[47]</a></sup></li>\n<li>1961: Emmy Award for "Program Achievement" for <i>Astaire Time</i></li>\n<li>1961: Voted Champion of Champions\xe2\x80\x94Best Television performer in annual television critics and columnists poll conducted by <i>Television Today</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Daily" title="Motion Picture Daily">Motion Picture Daily</a></i></li>\n<li>1965: The George Eastman Award<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/George_Eastman_Museum" title="George Eastman Museum">George Eastman House</a> for "outstanding contributions to motion pictures"</li>\n<li>1968: Inducted into the Hall of Fame of the <a href="/wiki/International_Best_Dressed_List" title="International Best Dressed List">International Best Dressed List</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>\n<li>1968: Nominated for an Emmy Award for <i>Musical Variety Program</i> for <i>The Fred Astaire Show</i></li>\n<li>1972: Named Musical Comedy Star of the Century by <i><a href="/wiki/Liberty_(general_interest_magazine)" title="Liberty (general interest magazine)">Liberty, "The Nostalgia Magazine"</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>\n<li>1972: Inducted into the <a href="/wiki/American_Theater_Hall_of_Fame" title="American Theater Hall of Fame">American Theater Hall of Fame</a><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>\n<li>1973: Subject of a Gala by the Film Society of <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Lincoln Center for the Performing Arts">Lincoln Center</a></li>\n<li>1975: Academy Award nomination for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Towering_Inferno" title="The Towering Inferno">The Towering Inferno</a></i></li>\n<li>1975: Golden Globe for "Best Supporting Actor", <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_di_Donatello" title="David di Donatello">David di Donatello</a> awards for <i>The Towering Inferno</i></li>\n<li>1978: <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> for "Best Actor\xe2\x80\x94Drama or Comedy Special" for <i>A Family Upside Down</i></li>\n<li>1978: Honored by the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Television_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences</a></li>\n<li>1978: First recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a></li>\n<li>1978: National Artist Award from the American National Theatre Association for "contributing immeasurably to the American Theatre"</li>\n<li>1981: The <a href="/wiki/List_of_lifetime_achievement_awards" title="List of lifetime achievement awards">Lifetime Achievement Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a></li>\n<li>1982: The Anglo-American Contemporary Dance Foundation announces creation of the Astaire Awards "to honor Fred Astaire and his sister Adele and to reward the achievement of an outstanding dancer or dancers"</li>\n<li>1987: The Capezio Dance Shoe Award (co-awarded with Rudolf Nureyev)</li>\n<li>1987: Inducted into the National Museum of Dance\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Dance_and_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Museum of Dance and Hall of Fame">Mr. &amp; Mrs. Cornelius Vanderbilt Whitney Hall of Fame</a> in Saratoga Springs, New York</li>\n<li>1989: Posthumous award of <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a></li>\n<li>1989: Posthumous induction into the <a href="/wiki/Television_Hall_of_Fame" title="Television Hall of Fame">Television Hall of Fame</a></li>\n<li>1991: Posthumous induction into the Ballroom Dancer\'s Hall of Fame</li>\n<li>1992: The <a href="/wiki/Dancing_House" title="Dancing House">Dancing House</a> in Prague is originally named "Fred and Ginger"</li>\n<li>1999: Posthumous award of <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Hall_of_Fame" title="Grammy Hall of Fame">Grammy Hall of Fame Award</a> for 1952 <a href="/wiki/The_Astaire_Story" title="The Astaire Story">The Astaire Story</a> album</li>\n<li>2000: Ava Astaire McKenzie unveils a plaque in honor of her father, erected by the citizens of <a href="/wiki/Lismore,_County_Waterford" title="Lismore, County Waterford">Lismore, County Waterford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a></li>\n<li>2000: "Fred Astaire", a song by <a href="/wiki/Lucky_Boys_Confusion" title="Lucky Boys Confusion">Lucky Boys Confusion</a></li>\n<li>2003: Referenced in the animated feature <i><a href="/wiki/The_Triplets_of_Belleville" title="The Triplets of Belleville">The Triplets of Belleville</a></i>, in which Astaire is eaten by his shoes after a fast-paced dance act</li>\n<li>2004: The "Adele and Fred Astaire Ballroom" added on the top floor of <a href="/wiki/Gottlieb_Storz_House" title="Gottlieb Storz House">Gottlieb Storz Mansion</a> in Astaire\'s hometown of Omaha<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>\n<li>2008: Life and work honored at <a href="/wiki/Oriel_College,_Oxford" title="Oriel College, Oxford">Oriel College</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>\n<li>2011, 2013: "Fred Astaire", a song, in a Portuguese and a later English version by <a href="/wiki/Clarice_Falc%C3%A3o" title="Clarice Falc\xc3\xa3o">Clarice Falc\xc3\xa3o</a></li>\n<li>2012: "Fred Astaire", a single and video by <a href="/wiki/San_Cisco" title="San Cisco">San Cisco</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fred_Astaire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Astaire was a <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservative</a> and a lifelong <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> supporter,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> though he never made his political views publicly known.<sup id="cite_ref-al._55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-al.-55">[55]</a></sup> Along with Bing Crosby, <a href="/wiki/George_Murphy" title="George Murphy">George Murphy</a>, Ginger Rogers, and others, he was a charter (founding) member of the Hollywood Republican Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> He was churchgoing, supportive of American military action, and dismissive of the increasing open sexuality in movies of the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-al._55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-al.-55">[55]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Always immaculately turned out, he and <a href="/wiki/Cary_Grant" title="Cary Grant">Cary Grant</a> were called "the best dressed actor[s] in American movies."<sup id="cite_ref-schwarz20070102_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schwarz20070102-57">[57]</a></sup> Astaire remained a male fashion icon even into his later years, eschewing his trademark top hat, white tie, and tails (for which he never really cared)<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> in favor of a breezy casual style of tailored sports jackets, colored shirts and slacks\xe2\x80\x94the latter usually held up by the idiosyncratic use of an old tie or silk scarf in place of a belt.</p>\n<p>Astaire married 25-year-old Phyllis Potter in 1933 (formerly Phyllis Livingston Baker; born 1908, died September 13, 1954), a <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>-born New York socialite and former wife of Eliphalet Nott Potter III (1906\xe2\x80\x931981), after pursuing her ardently for about two years, and despite his mother and sister\'s objections.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-12">[12]</a></sup> Phyllis\'s death from <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">lung cancer</a>, at the age of 46, ended 21 years of a blissful marriage and left Astaire devastated.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Astaire attempted to drop out of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Daddy_Long_Legs_(1955_film)" title="Daddy Long Legs (1955 film)">Daddy Long Legs</a></i> (1955), which he was in the process of filming, offering to pay the production costs to date, but was persuaded to stay.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In addition to Phyllis Potter\'s son, Eliphalet IV (known as Peter), the Astaires had two children. Fred, Jr. (born January 21, 1936), who appeared with his father in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Midas_Run" title="Midas Run">Midas Run</a></i> and later became a charter pilot and rancher instead of an actor. Their daughter Ava Astaire (born March 19, 1942; married Richard McKenzie) remains actively involved in promoting her late father\'s legacy. Fred Astaire was a devoted father and would often dance down the stairs of the family\'s home every morning, simply to entertain his two children.</p>\n<p>His friend, <a href="/wiki/David_Niven" title="David Niven">David Niven</a>, described him as "a pixie\xe2\x80\x94timid, always warm-hearted, with a penchant for schoolboy jokes." Astaire was a lifelong golf and <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">thoroughbred</a> horse racing enthusiast. In 1946 his horse <a href="/wiki/Triplicate_(horse)" title="Triplicate (horse)">Triplicate</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Cup_at_Santa_Anita_Stakes" title="Gold Cup at Santa Anita Stakes">Hollywood Gold Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Capistrano_Handicap" title="San Juan Capistrano Handicap">San Juan Capistrano Handicap</a>. He remained physically active well into his eighties. At age seventy-eight, he broke his left wrist while riding his grandson\'s skateboard.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG/200px-Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG" width="200" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG/300px-Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG/400px-Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="2736" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fred_Astaire_Grave.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nGrave of Fred Astaire, at Oakwood Memorial Park</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On June 24, 1980, at the age of 81, he married a second time. Robyn Smith (born August 14, 1944), was 45 years his junior and a jockey who rode for <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Gwynne_Vanderbilt_II" title="Alfred Gwynne Vanderbilt II">Alfred G. Vanderbilt II</a> and appeared on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> July 31, 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fred_Astaire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Astaire died of pneumonia on June 22, 1987, at the age of 88. Shortly before his death, Astaire said: "I didn\'t want to leave this world without knowing who my descendant was, thank you Michael"\xe2\x80\x94referring to <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> He was interred in the <a href="/wiki/Oakwood_Memorial_Park_Cemetery" title="Oakwood Memorial Park Cemetery">Oakwood Memorial Park Cemetery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chatsworth,_Los_Angeles" title="Chatsworth, Los Angeles">Chatsworth, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> One last request of his was to thank his fans for their years of support.</p>\n<p>Astaire\'s life has never been portrayed on film.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> He always refused permission for such portrayals, saying, "However much they offer me\xe2\x80\x94and offers come in all the time\xe2\x80\x94I shall not sell."<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Astaire\'s will included a clause requesting that no such portrayal ever take place; he commented, "It is there because I have no particular desire to have my life misinterpreted, which it would be."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span id="Stage.2C_film_and_television_work"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage,_film_and_television_work">Stage, film and television work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fred_Astaire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Stage, film and Theirs was the prototype of a gloriously happy marriage."</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Billman, p. 22: "Astaire\'s intense professionalism\xe2\x80\x94and the memory that Phyllis had wanted him to make the film\xe2\x80\x94made him report back for work. Caron remembered, "Fred used to sit down during a rehearsal and put his face in his towel and just cry."</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-61">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(Thomas p. 301) Astaire was awarded a life membership in the National Skateboard Society (Satchell p. 221). He remarked "Gene Kelly warned me not to be a damned fool, but I\'d seen the things those kids got up to on television doing all sorts of tricks. What a routine I could have worked up for a film sequence if they had existed a few years ago. Anyway I was practicing in my driveway."
